# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

The `loadConfiguration()` function orchestrates the loading:\\n- Loads the INI file using `ini.Load()` at line 1039\\n- Merges sections and keys from additional config files\\n- Each key-value pair is `getAuthorizedSettings()` which checks the user's permissions to view specific settings sections and keys\\n- Returns masked/redacted values so sensitive information is never exposed even with proper permissions\\n\\n### Configuration Sections\\n\\nDefault sections defined in `conf/defaults.ini` and handled by specific reader functions include:\\n- `[server]` - HTTP server configuration (read by `readServerSettings()` at line 1996)\\n- `[security]` - Security settings including secret keys and certificates (read by `readSecuritySettings()` at line 1688)\\n- `[auth]` - Authentication configuration (read by `readAuthSettings()` at line 1771)\\n- `[database]` - Database connection settings\\n- `[paths]` - File system paths for data, plugins, and provisioning\\n- Additional sections handled by dedicated setting files in `pkg/setting/setting_*.go`\\n\\n### Key Components\\n\\n**pkg/setting/setting.go** (Main Configuration Module):\\n- `Cfg` struct: Main configuration object with all parsed settings\\n- `Load()`: Entry point for configuration loading\\n- `loadConfiguration()`: Orchestrates the multi-step loading process\\n- `parseINIFile()`: Parses INI data into the Cfg struct\\n- `RedactedValue()` and `EnvKey()`: Utilities for masking and environment variable handling\\n\\n**pkg/setting/provider.go** (Settings Provider Interface):\\n- `Provider` interface: Abstract interface for accessing settings\\n- `OSSImpl`: OSS implementation of the provider\\n- `Current()`: Returns a SettingsBag with all settings (with values redacted for sensitive keys)\\n- `SettingsBag`: `cfg.appliedEnvOverrides` for logging purposes\\n\\n### Sensitive Value Masking\\n\\nThe `RedactedValue()` function (line 722) masks sensitive configuration values:\\n- Checks if a configuration key matches patterns for sensitive information: PASSWORD, SECRET, PROVIDER_CONFIG, PRIVATE_KEY, SECRET_KEY, CERTIFICATE, ACCOUNT_KEY, ENCRYPTION_KEY, VAULT_TOKEN, CLIENT_SECRET, ENTERPRISE_LICENSE, API_DB_PASS, and token-related keys (with regex support for TOKEN, ID_FORWARDING_TOKEN, AUTHENTICATION_TOKEN, AUTH_TOKEN, RENDERER_TOKEN, API_TOKEN, WEBHOOK_TOKEN, INSTALL_TOKEN)\\n- For sensitive keys, returns `RedactedPassword` constant (value: `\\\"*********\\\"`)\\n- Has exceptions for keys containing RUDDERSTACK, APPLICATION_INSIGHTS, or SENTRY (not masked even if they contain PASSWORD)\\n- For non-sensitive keys containing URLs, applies `RedactedURL()` which masks credentials in URLs\\n- The masking is applied in the settings provider's `Current()` method (provider.go:118-129) which calls `RedactedValue(EnvKey(...), value)` for each setting before returning them to API clients\\n\\n### API Endpoint for Settings (Sensitive Masking)\\n\\nThe `/api/admin/settings` endpoint is implemented in `pkg/api/admin.go:29` with the `AdminGetSettings()` function:\\n- Calls `hs.SettingsProvider.Current()` which returns a `SettingsBag` (map of section names to maps of key-value pairs)\\n- The settings provider (implemented in `provider.go`) automatically applies `RedactedValue()` to all values when returning them\\n- Access control is enforced via `getAuthorizedSettings()` which checks the user's permissions to view specific settings sections and keys\\n- Returns masked/redacted values so sensitive information is never exposed even with proper permissions\\n\\n### Configuration Sections\\n\\nDefault sections defined in `conf/defaults.ini` and handled by specific reader functions include:\\n- `[server]` - HTTP server configuration (read by `readServerSettings()` at line 1996)\\n- `[security]` - Security settings including secret keys and certificates (read by `readSecuritySettings()` at line 1688)\\n- `[auth]` - Authentication configuration (read by `readAuthSettings()` at line 1771)\\n- `[database]` - Database connection settings\\n- `[paths]` - File system paths for data, plugins, and provisioning\\n- Additional sections handled by dedicated setting files in `pkg/setting/setting_*.go`\\n\\n### Key Components\\n\\n**pkg/setting/setting.go** (Main Configuration Module):\\n- `Cfg` struct: Main configuration object with all parsed settings\\n- `Load()`: Entry point for configuration loading\\n- `loadConfiguration()`: Orchestrates the multi-step loading process\\n- `parseINIFile()`: Parses INI data into the Cfg struct\\n- `RedactedValue()` and `EnvKey()`: Utilities for masking and environment variable handling\\n\\n**pkg/setting/provider.go** (Settings Provider Interface):\\n- `Provider` interface: Abstract interface for accessing settings\\n- `OSSImpl`: OSS implementation of the provider\\n- `Current()`: Returns a SettingsBag with all settings (with values redacted for sensitive keys)\\n- `SettingsBag`: Type alias for `map[string]map[string]string` containing settings organized by section\\n\\n**pkg/setting/expanders.go** (Configuration Value Expansion):\\n- `expandConfig()`: Main function that expands variable references in configuration values\\n- `envExpander`: Expands environment variables like `${HOSTNAME}`\\n- `fileExpander`: Expands file paths and reads file contents like `$__file{/path/to/file}`\\n- Regex pattern: `\\\\$(|__\\\\w+){([^}]+)}` matches expansion patterns\\n\\n**pkg/api/admin.go** (Settings API):\\n- `AdminGetSettings()`: Handles GET /api/admin/settings endpoint\\n- Returns authorized, masked settings via the SettingsProvider\\n- Enforces fine-grained access control based on settings:read permissions\"\n}\n",
